\chapter{COLORIZATION STACK}


\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=0.85\textwidth]{/Users/wizard/.zpwr/docs/screenshots/art_data_stream.png}
\end{center}

\section{GRC: Generic Colorizer}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} GRC: GENERIC COLORIZER}\vspace{6pt}

Because monochrome ls is a crime against humanity.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} WHAT IS GRC?}\vspace{4pt}

grc wraps commands and adds color output via regex rules. It reads a config file that maps patterns to colors. Any command's output can be colorized. Zero modifications.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} GRC IN zpwrListNoClear}\vspace{4pt}

The fallback chain when listing files: 1. eza              preferred (color-scale, git status) 2. grc + ls         fallback (colorized via conf.gls) 3. Plain ls         last resort (no color config)


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} PLATFORM-SPECIFIC COMMANDS}\vspace{4pt}

MacOS:

\begin{codebox}
grc -c HOME/conf.gls gls -iFlhA --color=always\\
\end{codebox}

Linux:

\begin{codebox}
grc -c HOME/conf.gls ls -iFlhA --color=always\\
\end{codebox}

MacOS uses gls (GNU ls from coreutils) because BSD ls doesn't support all the flags. Linux uses native ls.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE conf.gls CONFIG}\vspace{4pt}

Custom color configuration for ls output, lives at:

\begin{codebox}
HOME/conf.gls\\
\end{codebox}

Maps file types, permissions, sizes to ANSI colors. Directories, executables, symlinks - all distinct colors.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} OTHER GRC TARGETS}\vspace{4pt}

grc can colorize almost any command: ping         latency numbers in color traceroute   hop-by-hop color coding make         errors red, warnings yellow gcc          compiler output colorized netstat      connection states highlighted diff         additions green, deletions red.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} GRC IN LOG COLORIZATION}\vspace{4pt}

\textbf{\$ZPWR\_SCRIPTS/colorLogger.sh} uses grc for system logs. tmux control windows show colorized live log output. TIP: If eza is missing and ls looks dull, install grc. It's the middle tier of zpwr's color fallback chain. One package, instant color for dozens of commands.


\vspace{16pt}

\section{Ponysay, Lolcat \& ASCII Art}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} PONYSAY, LOLCAT \& ASCII ART}\vspace{6pt}

Enterprise-grade cartoon horse infrastructure.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE ASCII ART TOOLCHAIN}\vspace{4pt}

ponysay    My Little Pony ASCII art (cowsay but fabulous) lolcat     rainbow gradient text output figlet     large ASCII text banners from font files cowsay     classic ASCII art speech bubbles toilet     another ASCII art text renderer zpwr combines all of these for its startup banner.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} \textbf{ZPWR} BANNER VERBS}\vspace{4pt}

zpwr bannerpony      hostname banner with ponysay zpwr bannerlolcat    ponysay + lolcat rainbow gradient zpwr bannernopony    banner without ponysay zpwr figletfonts     preview all installed figlet fonts Each verb calls a different autoloaded function:

\begin{codebox}
zpwrPonyBanner, zpwrBannerLolcat, zpwrNoPonyBanner\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE STARTUP BANNER}\vspace{4pt}

On shell startup, zpwrDarwinBanner / zpwrLinuxBanner fires. It picks a random figlet font each time via:

\begin{codebox}
ZPWR\_SCRIPTS/macOnly/figletRandomFontOnce.sh\\
\end{codebox}

\textbf{ZPWR\_BANNER}\_TYPE controls pony vs no-pony: ponies  -> zpwrBannerLolcat (rainbow horse) other   -> zpwrNoPonyBanner (figlet only)


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} BANNER CONTROL}\vspace{4pt}

\textbf{ZPWR\_BANNER}\_CLEARLIST  controls startup banner + ls display When true: clear screen, show banner, then zpwrListNoClear. When false: skip the banner entirely (fast startup).


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} FONT LOGGING}\vspace{4pt}

The random figlet font name is logged to:

\begin{codebox}
ZPWR\_LOGFILE\\
\end{codebox}

Want to know which font made that gorgeous banner? zpwr taillog  and look for the font name. Found one you love? Set it permanently in your config. REALITY CHECK: A rainbow pony greeting you on every terminal open is either peak engineering or peak insanity. zpwr does not distinguish between the two. Your hostname, rendered in ASCII art, by a cartoon horse. This is what unlimited power looks like.


\vspace{16pt}

\section{GRC, ccze \& the Color Pipeline}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} GRC, CCZE \& THE COLOR PIPELINE}\vspace{6pt}

Every byte of output deserves to be beautiful.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE FULL COLORIZATION STACK}\vspace{4pt}

zpwr has a color tool for every type of output: FILE LISTING eza (color-scale, git status) -> grc+ls -> plain ls FILE VIEWING bat (syntax highlighting) -> cat \textbf{ZPWR\_COLORIZER}=bat in \textbf{\$ZPWR\_ENV/.zpwr\_env.sh} LOG VIEWING ccze (log colorizer) -> plain tail zpwrTailLog pipes \$\textbf{ZPWR\_LOGFILE} through ccze. GIT DIFFS delta (syntax-aware diff) -> plain diff delta adds line numbers, word-level highlighting, and side-by-side view with Dracula theme.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} CCZE: LOG FILE COLORIZER}\vspace{4pt}

ccze parses log formats and applies semantic colors: timestamps, severity levels, PIDs, IP addresses. zpwr taillog  uses ccze for colorized log tailing. System logs become readable at a glance.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} COLOR TESTING VERBS}\vspace{4pt}

zpwr colortest       test terminal basic 16 colors zpwr colortest256    test full 256-color palette zpwr pygmentcolors   show all pygment color schemes zpwr colorsdiff      colorized side-by-side diff Use these to verify your terminal supports the full palette.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE FALLBACK PHILOSOPHY}\vspace{4pt}

Every color tool has a plain fallback: No eza? grc+ls. No grc? Plain ls. No bat? Cat. zpwr degrades gracefully. Color is never a hard dependency. SSH into a minimal server? Everything still works. Just less pretty. Function over form, always. THE RESULT: In a fully-equipped zpwr terminal: File listings glow. Logs are semantic. Diffs are surgical. Your eyes never have to parse raw monochrome again. The color pipeline is zpwr's cosmetic surgery department.


\vspace{16pt}


\chapter{HEALTH \& DIAGNOSTICS}


\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=0.85\textwidth]{/Users/wizard/.zpwr/docs/screenshots/zpwr_doctor_help.png}
\end{center}

\section{Startup Profile}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} STARTUP PROFILE}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // bench tells you HOW FAST. startup tells you WHERE the time goes. //}

zpwr bench measures total wall time over multiple iterations. zpwr startup gives a single-shot, per-function breakdown using zsh's built-in zprof profiler.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE VERB}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr startup               \# top 30 functions (default)\\
zpwr startup 50            \# top 50 functions\\
zpwr startup 100           \# full breakdown\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} HOW IT WORKS}\vspace{4pt}

1. Launches a fresh zsh with \textbf{ZPWR\_PROFILING}=true 2. zprof runs at the end of the init sequence 3. Output is captured and colorized by self-time: >= 10\%  RED       — hot path, optimize here >= 3\%   YELLOW    — warm, worth investigating >= 1\%   CYAN      — normal < 1\%    DIM       — negligible


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE PERFORMANCE QUARTET}\vspace{4pt}

zpwr bench    -> how fast is total startup? zpwr flame    -> ASCII flame chart of function hotspots zpwr startup  -> per-function zprof breakdown zpwr top      -> what is loaded right now?

Four verbs. Four perspectives. Your shell is transparent.


\vspace{16pt}

\section{Shell Lint}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} SHELL LINT}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // if it parses, it ships. but does it REALLY parse? //}

zpwr lint runs two levels of analysis on every zpwr file: syntax checking with zsh -n, and static analysis with shellcheck.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE VERB}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr lint                  \# run all checks\\
zpwr lint -z               \# zsh -n syntax check only\\
zpwr lint -s               \# shellcheck only\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} WHAT IT CHECKS}\vspace{4pt}

zsh -n (syntax check) Every file in autoload/common, autoload/darwin, autoload/linux, env/*.sh, env/*.zsh, install/.zshrc. This catches unmatched brackets, bad redirections, and broken quoting. Fast — no execution, just parsing.

shellcheck (static analysis) Every .sh and .zsh file in scripts/ and install/. Catches quoting bugs, unused variables, subshell pitfalls. Zsh-incompatible warnings are suppressed (SC1071 etc).


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} WHEN TO RUN IT}\vspace{4pt}

After editing any zpwr file. Before committing. Before pushing. Catch it at the gate, not in production.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} COMPANION VERBS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr doctor               \# broader health check\\
zpwr stale                \# find stale compiled files\\
zpwr recompile            \# rebuild .zwc files after fixes\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{16pt}

\section{Listening Ports}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} LISTENING PORTS}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // who is listening? and on which door? //}

zpwr ports wraps lsof to show every TCP port in LISTEN state with the process name, PID, user, and bind address.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE VERB}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr ports                 \# show all listening ports\\
zpwr ports 8080            \# filter to port 8080\\
zpwr ports -k 3000         \# kill whatever is on port 3000\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} COLOR CODING}\vspace{4pt}

Privileged ports (< 1024)    — RED These require root. Sshd on 22, httpd on 80. Common ports (< 10000)       — YELLOW Dev servers, databases. 3000, 5432, 8080. High ports (>= 10000)        — GREEN Ephemeral and user-space. Generally safe.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE KILL FLAG}\vspace{4pt}

zpwr ports -k 3000 finds the PID on port 3000 and sends SIGTERM. Shows process name before killing. Use when a dev server refuses to die.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} COMPANION VERBS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr lsof                 \# interactive fzf over all lsof output\\
zpwr ps                   \# grep through ps output\\
zpwr kill                 \# fzf kill from ps\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{16pt}

\section{Stale File Finder}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} STALE FILE FINDER}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // compiled cruft is invisible cruft. make it visible. //}

zpwr stale scans the entire zpwr tree for artifacts that have gone stale, orphaned, or broken.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE VERB}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr stale                 \# scan and report\\
zpwr stale -f              \# delete all stale files\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} WHAT IT FINDS}\vspace{4pt}

STALE .zwc Source file is newer than its compiled .zwc. Your shell is running yesterday's bytecode.

ORPHAN .zwc The source file was deleted but the .zwc remains. Dead weight taking up space and confusing zsh.

BROKEN SYMLINKS Symlinks pointing to files that no longer exist. Source of cryptic 'file not found' errors.

EMPTY CACHE FILES Zero-byte files in cache directories. Usually left behind by interrupted operations.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE FIX FLAG}\vspace{4pt}

zpwr stale -f deletes everything it finds in one pass. Follow up with zpwr recompile to rebuild .zwc files.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} WORKFLOW}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr stale                 \# see what is stale\\
zpwr stale -f              \# nuke the cruft\\
zpwr recompile             \# rebuild fresh .zwc files\\
zpwr doctor                \# verify everything is clean\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{16pt}

\section{Path Audit}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} PATH AUDIT}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // your \textbf{PATH} is your attack surface. audit it. //}

zpwr pathaudit inspects \textbf{PATH}, \textbf{FPATH}, and \textbf{MANPATH} for duplicates, missing directories, and world-writable entries.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE VERB}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr pathaudit             \# audit all three arrays\\
zpwr pathaudit -v          \# verbose: show every entry\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} WHAT IT CHECKS}\vspace{4pt}

DUPLICATES Same directory appearing more than once. Wastes hash lookups and obscures precedence. Fix: zpwr deduppaths.

MISSING DIRECTORIES \textbf{PATH} entry pointing to a dir that does not exist. Slows command lookup — zsh checks every entry.

WORLD-WRITABLE DIRECTORIES Any user can write to this directory. If it is in your \textbf{PATH}, an attacker can plant a malicious binary that shadows a real command. Security risk.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} ALL THREE ARRAYS}\vspace{4pt}

\textbf{PATH}     — command lookup for executables \textbf{FPATH}    — function autoload lookup for zsh \textbf{MANPATH}  — man page lookup for documentation.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} COMPANION VERBS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr doctor               \# broader health check (also checks paths)\\
zpwr deduppaths            \# remove duplicate entries\\
zpwr environmentcounts      \# count all env arrays\\
\end{codebox}

Doctor checks paths as part of a broader scan. Pathaudit goes deeper with world-writable detection.


\vspace{16pt}


\chapter{CREATIVE TOOLS}


\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=0.85\textwidth]{/Users/wizard/.zpwr/docs/screenshots/figlet_zpwr.png}
\end{center}

\section{The Matrix}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} THE MATRIX}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // not cmatrix. this is YOUR shell, raining. //}

zpwr matrix is an animated cyberpunk hacker story followed by an infinite ecosystem rain screensaver. Unlike cmatrix, it rains YOUR data — verb names, function names, aliases, env vars, and git repo names. Color-coded by type.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE STORY}\vspace{4pt}

ACT I    The Signal — the terminal underground survives ACT II   The Discovery — curl | zsh changes everything ACT III  The Power — bench, flame, doctor, gitwho ACT IV   The Choice — VS Code or zpwr matrix? Between acts: fake SSH sessions, encrypted transmissions, payload downloads with glitchy progress bars.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE FX}\vspace{4pt}

CRT scanlines       green sweep top-to-bottom VHS tracking        horizontal distortion bands Pixel corruption    spreading block static Screen tears        offset colored bands Figlet chaos        random fonts, random words, dissolve Progress bars       with random glitch spikes Pulse events        ecosystem facts flash across screen Scrolling ticker    horizontal stat crawl HUD overlay         live verb/alias/func/repo counters.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE RAIN COLORS}\vspace{4pt}

Green   verbs         cyan    functions yellow  aliases        magenta env vars red     git repos.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} USAGE}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr matrix                \# full story + rain\\
zpwr matrix -r             \# skip story, rain only\\
zpwr matrix -s 7           \# faster (1-9)\\
zpwr rain                  \# alias\\
zpwr screensaver           \# alias\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{16pt}


\chapter{INTROSPECTION}


\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=0.85\textwidth]{/Users/wizard/.zpwr/docs/screenshots/art_deep_dive.png}
\end{center}

\section{Command Resolver}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} COMMAND RESOLVER}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // what IS that command, really? //}

zpwr resolve traces a command through its full resolution chain. Unlike 'which' or 'type', it follows the entire path from alias to function to builtin to binary.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE VERB}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr resolve ll               \# where does ll go?\\
zpwr resolve ls cd git        \# trace multiple commands\\
zpwr resolve -a grep          \# show all type -a matches\\
zpwr which vim                \# alias for resolve\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} WHAT IT SHOWS}\vspace{4pt}

Aliases          expansion, then resolves first word.

\begin{codebox}
Functions        source file path, line count, verb mapping\\
\end{codebox}

Builtins         identified as builtin or reserved word Binaries         full path, symlink chain, file type Global aliases   detected and shown Suffix aliases   detected and shown.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} WHY NOT JUST 'which'?}\vspace{4pt}

'Which' shows one answer. 'type -a' shows all candidates. Neither follows the chain. If 'll' is an alias for 'eza' and 'eza' is a symlink to '../Cellar/eza/0.18\textbf{\textbf{/bin/eza}}', resolve shows the entire path from ll to the Mach-O binary.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} COMPANION VERBS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr exists                \# check if identifier is valid\\
zpwr deps                  \# function dependency graph\\
zpwr funcrank              \# rank functions by usage\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{16pt}


\chapter{CREATIVE TOOLS}


\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=0.85\textwidth]{/Users/wizard/.zpwr/docs/screenshots/figlet_zpwr.png}
\end{center}

\section{Fortune Cookies}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} FORTUNE COOKIES}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // wisdom from the digital underground //}

zpwr fortune displays a random hacker quote rendered in a random figlet font with neon colors. 40 curated quotes from legends and original \textbf{ZPWR} wisdom.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE VERB}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr fortune                \# random quote, random font\\
zpwr fortune -p             \# plain text with box frame\\
zpwr fortune -f doom        \# force doom font\\
zpwr wisdom                 \# alias\\
zpwr quote                  \# alias\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE QUOTES}\vspace{4pt}

Linus Torvalds    "Talk is cheap. Show me the code." Brian Kernighan   "Controlling complexity is the essence..." Grace Hopper      "The most dangerous phrase is..." \textbf{ZPWR}              "Home is where the .zshrc is." MenkeTechnologies  "Aliases are love letters to your future self." ...and 35 more.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE FONTS}\vspace{4pt}

Randomly selected from: cyberlarge, cybermedium, doom, slant, speed, banner, standard. Each quote picks a keyword for large figlet rendering, full quote below.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} USE CASES}\vspace{4pt}

- Add to .zshrc for a fortune on every new shell - Pipe to lolcat: zpwr fortune -p | lolcat - Use as a tmux status-right: too slow, but fun to try


\vspace{16pt}


\chapter{THE SEARCH ENGINE}


\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=0.85\textwidth]{/Users/wizard/.zpwr/docs/screenshots/figlet_scan.png}
\end{center}

\section{The Learning System}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} THE LEARNING SYSTEM}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // your shell remembers what you learn //}

The zsh-learn plugin turns your shell into a persistent knowledge base backed by MySQL. Save commands, search them, quiz yourself, and build a personal learning collection.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} CORE VERBS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr learn                  \# save a learning entry\\
zpwr searchl                \# search the collection\\
zpwr quiz                   \# quiz yourself\\
zpwr quizall                \# quiz all entries\\
zpwr redo                   \# redo last search as SQL update\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} SEARCH VARIANTS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr se                     \# basic search\\
zpwr see                    \# category search\\
zpwr seee                   \# timestamp search\\
zpwr ser                    \# random search\\
zpwr sef                    \# search into fzf\\
zpwr searchall              \# entire collection into fzf\\
zpwr searchfull             \# entire collection into fzf\\
zpwr searchle               \# category search (alias for see)\\
zpwr searchlee              \# timestamp search (alias for seee)\\
zpwr learnsearch            \# search the collection\\
zpwr rsql                   \# redo into vim\\
zpwr redosql                \# redo into vim\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} MANAGEMENT}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr learndel               \# delete entry\\
zpwr learndelete            \# delete entry (alias)\\
zpwr delid                  \# delete by ID\\
zpwr editl                  \# edit entry by ID\\
zpwr getlearn               \# get all entries\\
zpwr learnget               \# get all entries\\
zpwr createlearningcollection \# create MySQL table\\
zpwr droplearningcollection   \# drop MySQL table\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} HOW IT WORKS}\vspace{4pt}

Entries are stored in a MySQL database (configurable via \$\textbf{ZPWR\_SCHEMA}\_NAME and \$\textbf{ZPWR\_TABLE}\_NAME). Each entry has a category, timestamp, and content. The quiz system pulls random entries and tests your recall.

Plugin: MenkeTechnologies/zsh-learn.


\vspace{16pt}


\chapter{BATCH OPERATIONS}


\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=0.85\textwidth]{/Users/wizard/.zpwr/docs/screenshots/art_override.png}
\end{center}

\section{Git Repo Cache System}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} GIT REPO CACHE SYSTEM}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // index every repo on your machine. operate on all of them. //}

The zsh-git-repo-cache plugin scans your entire filesystem for git repos, caches the list, and lets you search, filter, and broadcast commands across all of them.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} CACHE GENERATION}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr regengitrepocache      \# scan filesystem with fd/find\\
zpwr regengitdirtyrepocache  \# scan only dirty repos\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} SEARCH \& BROWSE}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr gitrepos               \# all repos into fzf\\
zpwr gitreposclean          \# clean repos into fzf\\
zpwr gitreposdirty          \# dirty repos into fzf\\
zpwr gitreposlist           \# list all repos (no fzf)\\
zpwr gitreposcleanlist      \# list clean repos\\
zpwr gitreposdirtylist      \# list dirty repos\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} CACHED VARIANTS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr gitreposcleancache     \# clean repos from cache\\
zpwr gitreposdirtycache     \# dirty repos from cache\\
zpwr gitreposcleancachelist  \# list clean from cache\\
zpwr gitreposdirtycachelist  \# list dirty from cache\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} BATCH OPERATIONS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr gitreposexec <cmd>      \# run cmd in all cached repos\\
zpwr gitreposdirtyexec <cmd> \# run cmd in dirty repos\\
zpwr gitreposcleanexec <cmd> \# run cmd in clean repos\\
zpwr gitwho                 \# contributor stats across all repos\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} CACHE FILES}\vspace{4pt}

\$\textbf{ZPWR\_ALL}\_GIT\_DIRS       — all repos \$\textbf{ZPWR\_ALL}\_GIT\_DIRS\_CLEAN — clean repos only \$\textbf{ZPWR\_ALL}\_GIT\_DIRS\_DIRTY — dirty repos only.

Plugin: MenkeTechnologies/zsh-git-repo-cache.


\vspace{16pt}


\chapter{FZF ARCHITECTURE}


\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=0.85\textwidth]{/Users/wizard/.zpwr/docs/screenshots/figlet_scan.png}
\end{center}

\section{FZF Brew \& Chrome}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} FZF BREW \& CHROME}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // fuzzy finding extends to your package manager and browser //}

The fzf-zsh-plugin adds fzf interfaces to Homebrew package management and Chrome browser data.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} HOMEBREW VERBS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr brewinstall            \# fzf install formula\\
zpwr brewuninstall          \# fzf uninstall formula\\
zpwr brewcaskinstall        \# fzf install cask\\
zpwr brewcaskuninstall      \# fzf uninstall cask\\
zpwr brewupdate             \# fzf update formula\\
\end{codebox}

Each command pipes the available packages into fzf with multi-select. Pick one or many, then install/remove in one shot. No more googling package names.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} CHROME VERBS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr chromehistory          \# search Chrome history in fzf\\
zpwr chromebookmarks        \# search Chrome bookmarks in fzf\\
\end{codebox}

Reads Chrome's SQLite databases directly. Select a URL from fzf and open it in the browser.

Plugin: MenkeTechnologies/fzf-zsh-plugin.


\vspace{16pt}


\chapter{THE GIT DIMENSION}


\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=0.85\textwidth]{/Users/wizard/.zpwr/docs/screenshots/art_data_stream.png}
\end{center}

\section{Git Add-Commit-Push}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} GIT ADD-COMMIT-PUSH}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // 318 aliases for the git power user //}

The zsh-git-acp plugin provides 318 aliases that collapse multi-step git workflows into single commands.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE GACP PATTERN}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
gacp "message"              \# git add -A, commit, push\\
gac "message"               \# git add -A, commit (no push)\\
gcp                          \# git commit, push\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} BRANCH SHORTCUTS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
gcm                          \# git checkout main\\
gcb <branch>                 \# git checkout -b <branch>\\
gbd <branch>                 \# git branch -d <branch>\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} \textbf{ZPWR} INTEGRATION}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr gitcommit "msg"        \# commit and push with message\\
zpwr gitcommitcount          \# count commits in current repo\\
\end{codebox}

The full alias list is enormous — 318 combinations of git operations compressed into 2-4 character shortcuts. Most follow the pattern: g + operation letter(s).

Plugin: MenkeTechnologies/zsh-git-acp.


\vspace{16pt}


\chapter{NETWORK \& CONTAINERS}

\section{Docker \& Container Aliases}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} DOCKER \& CONTAINER ALIASES}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // 148 aliases for the containerized world //}

The zsh-docker-aliases plugin provides 148 aliases for Docker and Docker Compose operations.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} DOCKER SHORTCUTS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
dps                          \# docker ps\\
dpsa                         \# docker ps -a\\
di                           \# docker images\\
drm                          \# docker rm\\
drmi                         \# docker rmi\\
dex                          \# docker exec -it\\
dl                           \# docker logs -f\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} DOCKER COMPOSE}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
dcu                          \# docker compose up -d\\
dcd                          \# docker compose down\\
dcl                          \# docker compose logs -f\\
dcr                          \# docker compose restart\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} \textbf{ZPWR} INTEGRATION}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr dockerwipe              \# nuke all images/containers\\
zpwr dfimage <ID>            \# extract Dockerfile from image\\
\end{codebox}

Plugin: MenkeTechnologies/zsh-docker-aliases.

\chapter{ZINIT \& PLUGIN SYSTEM}


\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=0.85\textwidth]{/Users/wizard/.zpwr/docs/screenshots/art_system_core.png}
\end{center}

\section{The Plugin Ecosystem}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} THE PLUGIN ECOSYSTEM}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // 30+ custom plugins from MenkeTechnologies //}

\textbf{ZPWR} loads approximately 95 plugins via zinit. Over 30 are custom MenkeTechnologies creations that extend zpwr with additional verbs, aliases, completions, and integrations.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} KEY PLUGINS}\vspace{4pt}

Zsh-learn              60 verbs, MySQL learning DB zsh-git-repo-cache    20 verbs, filesystem repo index fzf-zsh-plugin        14 verbs, brew/chrome fzf zsh-git-acp           318 aliases, git workflows zsh-docker-aliases    148 aliases, Docker shortcuts zsh-openshift-aliases 106 aliases, OpenShift zsh-expand            spell correct, abbreviation expand zsh-more-completions  many thousands of tab completions zsh-cargo-completion  32 Rust/Cargo aliases zsh-travis            8 functions, CI integration zsh-nginx             nginx management forgit                fzf-powered git (add, diff, log) zsh-z                 frecency directory jumping fzf-tab               fzf-powered tab completion zconvey               cross-session communication.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} CONDITIONAL LOADING}\vspace{4pt}

Plugins for docker, dotnet, kubectl, ngrok, rails, and systemctl only load if those commands exist. No bloat on machines without those tools.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} DEFERRED LOADING}\vspace{4pt}

All plugins load with zinit wait'' ice — deferred after the prompt appears. Only powerlevel10k loads synchronously for instant prompt.


\vspace{16pt}


\chapter{TIPS, TRICKS \& EASTER EGGS}

\section{Alias Cheat Sheet}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} ALIAS CHEAT SHEET}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // the short names you will actually use //}

Many zpwr verbs have short aliases. These are the ones worth memorizing — one or two keystrokes that replace entire workflows.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} DIAGNOSTICS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr doc          = doctor       zpwr zprof      = startup\\
zpwr check        = lint         zpwr audit      = pathaudit\\
zpwr cruft        = stale        zpwr rank       = funcrank\\
zpwr benchmark    = bench        zpwr dashboard  = top\\
zpwr heatmap      = flame        zpwr instrument = trace\\
zpwr flamechart   = flame        zpwr checkup    = doctor\\
zpwr callers      = deps         zpwr aliasusage = aliasrank\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} MONITORING}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr snap         = snapshot     zpwr load       = restore\\
zpwr rerun        = replay       zpwr onchange   = watch\\
zpwr book         = study\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} CREATIVE}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr rain         = matrix       zpwr wisdom     = fortune\\
zpwr quote        = fortune      zpwr screensaver= matrix\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} GIT}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr who          = gitwho       zpwr gitcontribs= gitwho\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} INTROSPECTION}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr which        = resolve      zpwr whatis     = resolve\\
zpwr today        = timeline     zpwr activity   = timeline\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} LOGGING}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr logs         = taillog\\
\end{codebox}

\chapter{EMACS DIMENSION}

\section{Emacs Integration}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} EMACS INTEGRATION}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // 29 verbs for the church of emacs //}

Every file operation in \textbf{ZPWR} has an emacs variant. Open, edit, search, and navigate — all wired to emacsclient.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} OPEN \& EDIT}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr emacsall              \# emacs all zpwr files for :argdo\\
zpwr emacsallserver        \# emacs all zpwr files via server\\
zpwr emacsalledit          \# emacs edit 1 or more configs\\
zpwr emacsautoload         \# emacs all autoloads :argdo\\
zpwr emacsscripts          \# emacs all zpwr scripts for :argdo\\
zpwr emacsscriptedit       \# emacs edit 1 or more scripts\\
zpwr emacszpwr             \# emacs zpwr dir\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} CONFIG \& TOKENS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr emacsconfig           \# emacs all zpwr configs\\
zpwr emacsemacsconfig      \# emacs edit emacs zpwr configs\\
zpwr emacstokens           \# emacs the .tokens.sh file\\
zpwr emacstests            \# emacs edit all zpwr tests\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} NAVIGATION}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr emacscd               \# emacs edit and cd to first dir\\
zpwr emacsrecent           \# emacs edit most recent editor files\\
zpwr emacsrecentcd         \# cd and emacs edit most recent files\\
zpwr emacsrecentsudo       \# sudo emacs edit most recent files\\
zpwr emacsrecentsudocd     \# cd and sudo emacs most recent files\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} SEARCH}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr emacsfilesearch       \# emacs a file in a sub dir\\
zpwr emacsfilesearchedit   \# edit emacs a file in a sub dir\\
zpwr emacsfindsearch       \# emacs find drive for file\\
zpwr emacsfindsearchedit   \# emacs edit find drive for file\\
zpwr emacslocatesearch     \# emacs accept locate drive for file\\
zpwr emacslocatesearchedit \# emacs edit locate drive for file\\
zpwr emacswordsearch       \# emacs a file in a sub dir by word\\
zpwr emacswordsearchedit   \# edit emacs a file by word\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} TAGS \& PLUGINS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr emacsctags            \# emacs zpwr ctags tags\\
zpwr emacsgtags            \# emacs zpwr GNU global tags\\
zpwr emacsgtagsedit        \# emacs edit zpwr GNU global tags\\
zpwr emacsplugincount      \# total number of emacs plugins\\
zpwr emacspluginlist       \# total list of emacs plugins\\
\end{codebox}

\section{Vim Integration}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} VIM INTEGRATION}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // 35 verbs for the vim faithful //}

The vim verb family mirrors emacs with full parity. Open, edit, search, navigate — all wired to vim/nvim.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} OPEN \& EDIT}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr vimall               \# vim all zpwr files for :argdo\\

zpwr vimautoload           \# vim all autoloads :argdo\\

zpwr vimscriptedit         \# vim edit 1 or more scripts\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} CONFIG \& TOKENS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr vimconfig             \# edit all zpwr configs\\
zpwr vimemacsconfig        \# vim edit emacs zpwr configs\\
zpwr vimtokens             \# vim the .tokens.sh file\\
zpwr vimtests              \# edit all zpwr tests\\
zpwr vrc                   \# vimrc vim session\\
zpwr brc                   \# shell aliases file vim session\\
zpwr trc                   \# tmux.conf vim session\\
zpwr zrc                   \# zshrc vim session\\
zpwr tokens                \# vim the .tokens.sh file\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} NAVIGATION}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr vimcd                 \# vim edit and cd to first dir\\
zpwr vimrecent             \# vim edit most recent editor files\\
zpwr vimrecentcd           \# cd and vim edit most recent files\\
zpwr vimrecentsudo         \# sudo vim edit most recent files\\
zpwr vimrecentsudocd       \# cd and sudo vim most recent files\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} SEARCH}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr vimsearch             \# search vim keybindings\\
zpwr vimfilesearch         \# vim a file in a sub dir\\
zpwr vimfilesearchedit     \# edit vim a file in a sub dir\\
zpwr vimfindsearch         \# vim accept find drive for file\\
zpwr vimfindsearchedit     \# vim edit find drive for file\\
zpwr vimlocatesearch       \# vim accept locate drive for file\\
zpwr vimlocatesearchedit   \# vim edit locate drive for file\\
zpwr vimwordsearch         \# vim a file in a sub dir by word\\
zpwr vimwordsearchedit     \# edit vim a file by word\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} TAGS, PLUGINS \& VIMINFO}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr vimctags              \# vim zpwr ctags tags\\
zpwr vimgtags              \# vim zpwr GNU global tags\\
zpwr vimgtagsedit          \# vim edit zpwr GNU global tags\\
zpwr vimplugincount        \# total number of vim plugins\\
zpwr vimpluginlist         \# total list of vim plugins\\
zpwr catviminfo            \# cat custom vim info file\\
zpwr catrecentfviminfo     \# cat recentf then custom vim info\\
zpwr catnviminforecentf    \# cat custom vim info then recentf\\
\end{codebox}

\chapter{THE GIT DIMENSION}


\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=0.85\textwidth]{/Users/wizard/.zpwr/docs/screenshots/art_data_stream.png}
\end{center}

\section{Git Operations Reference}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} GIT OPERATIONS REFERENCE}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // 33 verbs for git mastery //}

Core git verbs for commits, config, history rewriting, contributor stats, and multi-repo operations.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} COMMIT \& PUSH}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr gitcommit             \# commit and push with arg message\\
zpwr gitcommitcount        \# count commits in current repo\\
zpwr gitcommits            \# search git commits with fzf\\
zpwr clone                 \# clone and cd to arg\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} CONFIG \& IGNORES}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr gitconfig             \# edit git config file\\
zpwr gitglobalconfig       \# edit git config file\\
zpwr gitignore             \# EDITOR \textasciitilde{}/.git/info/exclude\\
zpwr gitignores            \# edit git ignores file\\
zpwr gitglobalignores      \# edit git ignores file\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} EMAIL \& HISTORY REWRITING}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr gitemail              \# change email with git filter-branch\\
zpwr gitcemail             \# change committer email\\
zpwr gitaemail             \# change author email\\
zpwr gitclearcommit        \# remove matching commits from history\\
zpwr gitclearcache         \# clear old git refs and objects\\
zpwr gitclearfile          \# rm file from all git refs/objects\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} STATS \& INFO}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr gitcontribcount       \# count git contributions by author\\
zpwr gitcontribcountdirs   \# contributions by author for dirs\\
zpwr gitcontribcountlines  \# count lines contributed by author\\
zpwr gittotallines         \# total line count of git files\\
zpwr gitlargest            \# show largest files stored by git\\
zpwr gitremotes            \# list all git remotes\\
zpwr gitdir                \# check if pwd is git dir\\
zpwr gitwho                \# aggregate contributor stats\\
zpwr gitsearch             \# search for regex in git log\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} MULTI-REPO \& TAGS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr gitforalldir          \# run cmd in all git dirs\\
zpwr gitfordirdevelop      \# git wipe to develop in git dirs\\
zpwr gitfordirmain         \# git wipe to main in git dirs\\
zpwr gitupdatefordir       \# run git updates in all git dirs\\
zpwr gitzfordir            \# git wipe on branch in git dirs\\
zpwr gitzfordirdevelop     \# z and git wipe to develop\\
zpwr gitzfordirmain        \# z and git wipe to main\\
zpwr gitupdatetag          \# print tag and latest msg\\
zpwr gitedittag            \# print tag to BUFFER\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{16pt}

\section{GitHub \& Travis CI}


\vspace{10pt}

\section{Navigation Verbs}


\vspace{10pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // 39 ways to get where you are going //}

Navigate the filesystem, \textbf{ZPWR} directories, and frecency ranked locations with precision.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} DIRECTORY MOVEMENT}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr cd                    \# cd to directory arg\\
zpwr f                     \# cd to directory arg\\
zpwr forward               \# cd to directory arg\\
zpwr fwd                   \# cd to directory arg\\
zpwr cdup                  \# cd up tree to directory arg\\
zpwr r                     \# cd up tree to directory arg\\
zpwr reverse               \# cd up tree to directory arg\\
zpwr rvs                   \# cd up tree to directory arg\\
zpwr catcd                 \# cat and cd to first dir\\
zpwr clone                 \# clone and cd to arg\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} \textbf{ZPWR} \textbf{HOME} DIRECTORIES}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr home                  \# go to ZPWR\\
zpwr homeautoload          \# go to ZPWR\_AUTOLOAD\\
zpwr homeautoloadcommon    \# go to ZPWR\_AUTOLOAD\_COMMON\\
zpwr homecomps             \# go to ZPWR\_COMPS\\
zpwr homeenv               \# go to ZPWR\_ENV\\
zpwr homeexercism          \# cd to HOME/Exercism\\
zpwr homeinstall           \# go to ZPWR\_INSTALL\\
zpwr homelocal             \# go to ZPWR\_LOCAL\\
zpwr homescripts           \# go to ZPWR\_SCRIPTS\\
zpwr hometest              \# go to ZPWR\_TEST\\
zpwr hometests             \# go to ZPWR\_TEST\\
zpwr hometmux              \# go to ZPWR\_TMUX\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} \textbf{ZPWR} SUBDIRECTORIES}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr autoload              \# cd to autoload directory\\
zpwr comps                 \# cd to completion directory\\
zpwr completions           \# cd to completion directory\\
zpwr forked                \# cd to ZPWR\_FORKED\_DIR\\
zpwr fp                    \# cd to ZPWR\_FORKED\_DIR\\
zpwr hidden                \# go to ZPWR\_HIDDEN\_DIR\\
zpwr plugins               \# cd to ZSH\_CUSTOM/plugins\\
zpwr repo                  \# cd to ZPWR\_REPO\_NAME\\
zpwr scripts               \# cd to scripts directory\\
zpwr web                   \# cd to web dir\\
zpwr zp                    \# cd to ZPWR\_REPO\_NAME\\
zpwr zpwr                  \# cd to ZPWR\_REPO\_NAME\\
zpwr zpz                   \# cd to repo, checkout, rebase, push\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} FRECENCY \& FZF}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr z                     \# cd to z frecency ranked dir\\
zpwr zcd                   \# list then cd to z ranked dir\\
zpwr dirsearch             \# cd to a sub dir via fzf\\
\end{codebox}

\section{Regen \& Compile}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} REGEN \& COMPILE}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // 24 verbs to rebuild the world //}

Regenerate caches, recompile zsh word code, and rebuild tags. The engine room of \textbf{ZPWR} maintenance.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} REGEN CACHES}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr regen                 \# regen caches except git drive search\\
zpwr regenall              \# regen all caches\\
zpwr regenpdf              \# regenerate encyclopedia PDF\\
zpwr regenenvcache         \# regen search env to zpwrEnv files\\
zpwr regengitrepocache     \# regen list of all git repos\\
zpwr regengitdirtyrepocache\# regen list of dirty git repos\\
zpwr regenhistory          \# regen HISTFILE\\
zpwr regenkeybindings      \# regen all keybindings cache\\
zpwr regenconfiglinks      \# regen sym links to HOME\\
zpwr regenpowerline        \# regen powerline sym link\\
zpwr regenzsh              \# regen compsys cache\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} REGEN TAGS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr regengtags            \# regen gtags files to HOME\\
zpwr regenctags            \# regen ctags files to HOME\\
zpwr regengtagspygments    \# regen GNU gtags with pygments\\
zpwr regengtagstype        \# regen GNU gtags with specified parser\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} COMPILE \& DECOMPILE}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr compile               \# recompile all cache comps\\
zpwr compilefpath          \# recompile all fpath cache comps\\
zpwr compilefiles          \# recompile all files cache comps\\
zpwr recompile             \# recompile all cache comps\\
zpwr recompilefpath        \# recompile all fpath cache comps\\
zpwr recompilefiles        \# recompile all files cache comps\\
zpwr refreshzwc            \# delete then regen compiled zsh word code\\
zpwr decompile             \# delete all cache comps\\
zpwr uncompile             \# delete all cache comps\\
\end{codebox}

\end{codebox}

\vspace{12pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr a                     \# banner, counts, clean, refresh, test, update\\
zpwr all                   \# banner, counts, clean, refresh, test, update\\
\end{codebox}

\chapter{BUILD SYSTEM}

\end{center}

\section{Update System}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} UPDATE SYSTEM}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // 6 verbs to stay current //}

Keep \textbf{ZPWR}, its dependencies, and zinit plugins up to date. From surgical single-dep pulls to full system updates.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} CONFIG UPDATES}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr update                \# update zpwr custom configs\\
zpwr updatepull            \# pull latest config from repo\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} DEPENDENCY UPDATES}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr updatedeps            \# update all dependencies\\
zpwr updatedepsclean       \# update all dependencies then clean\\
zpwr updatezinit           \# update zinit dependencies\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} FULL UPDATE}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr updateall             \# update zpwr configs and all deps\\
\end{codebox}

Typical workflow: zpwr updateall pulls the latest configs, updates brew/pip/npm/gem/zinit, and refreshes caches. Run zpwr updatedepsclean afterward to reclaim disk space from stale packages.

\chapter{THE LOGGING SYSTEM}


\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=0.85\textwidth]{/Users/wizard/.zpwr/docs/screenshots/art_data_stream.png}
\end{center}

\section{Logging System}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} LOGGING SYSTEM}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // 12 verbs for structured observability //}

\textbf{ZPWR} has a four-level logging system: trace, debug, info, error. Each level writes to file or console.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} LOG TO FILE}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr logtrace              \# log trace to ZPWR\_LOGFILE\\
zpwr logdebug              \# log debug to ZPWR\_LOGFILE\\
zpwr loginfo               \# log info to ZPWR\_LOGFILE\\
zpwr logerror              \# log error to ZPWR\_LOGFILE\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} LOG TO CONSOLE}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr logtraceconsole       \# log trace to console\\
zpwr logdebugconsole       \# log debug to console\\
zpwr loginfoconsole        \# log info to console\\
zpwr logerrorconsole       \# log error to console\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} LOG MANAGEMENT}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr taillog               \# colorized tail of ZPWR\_LOGFILE\\
zpwr logs                  \# colorized tail of ZPWR\_LOGFILE\\
zpwr cleanlog              \# clear ZPWR\_LOGFILE\\
zpwr logincount            \# count of logins by user\\
\end{codebox}

Log levels from most verbose to least: TRACE >   DEBUG >   INFO >   ERROR.

\vspace{12pt}

zpwr subcommandsedit       \# edit subcommands for zpwr <tab>\\
zpwr subcommandsfzf        \# fzf subcommands for zpwr <tab>\\
zpwr subcommandslist       \# list subcommands for zpwr <tab>\\
zpwr verbs                 \# run subcommands for zpwr <tab>\\
zpwr verbscount            \# number of verbs\\
zpwr verbsedit             \# edit subcommands for zpwr <tab>\\
zpwr verbsfzf              \# fzf subcommands for zpwr <tab>\\
zpwr verbslist             \# list subcommands for zpwr <tab>\\
zpwr help                  \# list subcommands with color\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} MISC INTROSPECTION}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr tty                   \# print current tty\\
zpwr relpath               \# get relative path to PWD\\
zpwr printmap              \# pretty print maps\\
\end{codebox}

\chapter{APPENDIX A: KEYBINDING REFERENCE}


\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=0.85\textwidth]{/Users/wizard/.zpwr/docs/screenshots/art_the_grid.png}
\end{center}

\section{Tmux Prefix Keys: Navigation \& Panes}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} TMUX PREFIX KEYS: NAVIGATION \& PANES}\vspace{6pt}

pane traversal, splitting, resizing. the grid of power.\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} PANE SELECTION (hjkl repeatable):}\vspace{4pt}

prefix h              select pane left\\
prefix j              select pane down\\
prefix k              select pane up\\
prefix l              select pane right\\
prefix ;              last-pane (toggle to previous)\\
prefix o              select next pane in order\\
prefix q              display-panes (5s timeout)\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} PANE RESIZE (HJKL repeatable, 5 cells):}\vspace{4pt}

prefix H              resize pane left 5\\
prefix J              resize pane down 5\\
prefix K              resize pane up 5\\
prefix L              resize pane right 5\\
prefix Ctrl-Up/Down   resize pane by 1\\
prefix Alt-Up/Down    resize pane by 5\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} PANE SPLITTING:}\vspace{4pt}

prefix -              split vertical (same dir)\\
prefix \textbackslash{}\textbackslash{}              split horizontal (same dir)\\
prefix "              split vertical (default dir)\\
prefix \%              split horizontal (default dir)\\
prefix |              split horizontal\\
prefix \_              split vertical\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} PANE OPERATIONS:}\vspace{4pt}

prefix z              zoom/unzoom current pane\\
prefix !              break pane into own window\\
prefix x              kill current pane\\
prefix m              mark current pane\\
prefix +              split vertical then close prev pane\\
prefix Y              split vertical then close prev pane\\
prefix \{              rotate window\\
prefix \}              swap pane down\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} ARROW KEY SELECTION:}\vspace{4pt}

prefix Up/Down        select pane up/down\\
prefix Left/Right     select pane left/right\\
Alt-Up/Down           select pane (root table, no prefix)\\
Alt-Left/Right        select pane (root table, no prefix)\\

All hjkl/HJKL bindings are repeatable (-r flag).\\
Arrow keys in root table work without prefix for speed.\\

\begin{codebox}
// the wizard navigates panes by instinct\\
// hjkl is muscle memory, arrows are for civilians\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{16pt}

\section{Tmux Prefix Keys: Windows \& Sessions}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} TMUX PREFIX KEYS: WINDOWS \& SESSIONS}\vspace{6pt}

window management, session juggling, the multiplexer core.\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} WINDOW CREATION \& SELECTION:}\vspace{4pt}

prefix c              new window\\
prefix a              last-window (toggle to previous)\\
prefix 0-9            select window by number\\
prefix '              select window by index prompt\\
prefix n              next window (repeatable)\\
prefix p              previous window (repeatable)\\
prefix Ctrl-n         next window\\
prefix Ctrl-p         previous window\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} WINDOW OPERATIONS:}\vspace{4pt}

prefix ,              rename current window\\
prefix \&              kill window (with confirm)\\
prefix .              move window to target\\
prefix f              find window by name\\
prefix w              choose-tree window view\\
prefix i              display-message (window info)\\
prefix t              clock-mode\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} SESSION MANAGEMENT:}\vspace{4pt}

prefix \$              rename current session\\
prefix (              switch to previous client (repeatable)\\
prefix )              switch to next client (repeatable)\\
prefix d              detach client\\
prefix s              choose-tree session view\\
prefix Ctrl-z         suspend client\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} RELOAD \& PERSIST:}\vspace{4pt}

prefix r              reload tmux config + display confirmation\\
prefix Ctrl-s         save session (tmux-resurrect)\\
prefix Ctrl-r         restore session (tmux-resurrect)\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} ROOT TABLE SHORTCUTS:}\vspace{4pt}

Ctrl-\textbackslash{}\textbackslash{}               switch to next client (no prefix)\\
Ctrl-]               switch to prev client (no prefix)\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} META:}\vspace{4pt}

prefix ?              list all keys\\
prefix :              command prompt\\
prefix /              describe a key binding\\
prefix \textasciitilde{}              show messages\\

\begin{codebox}
// sessions are parallel universes\\
// the wizard keeps many realities open at once\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{16pt}

\section{Tmux Prefix Keys: Layouts \& Pane Configs}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} TMUX PREFIX KEYS: LAYOUTS \& PANE CONFIGS}\vspace{6pt}

preconfigured pane arrangements. instant workspaces.\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} \textbf{ZPWR} LAYOUT PRESETS:}\vspace{4pt}

prefix D              control-window layout\\
prefix E              four vertical panes\\
prefix F              four panes layout\\
prefix G              eight panes layout\\
prefix O              sixteen panes layout\\
prefix R              thirty-two panes REPL layout\\
prefix T              config files layout\\
prefix M              learn layout\\

Each layout sources a conf file from \textbf{\$ZPWR/tmux/}:\\
D -> control-window.conf\\
E -> fourVertical.conf\\
F -> four-panes.conf\\
G -> eight-panes.conf\\
O -> sixteen-panes.conf\\
R -> thirtytwo-panes-repl.conf\\
T -> config-files.conf\\
M -> learn.conf\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} SYNCHRONIZE \& CUSTOMIZE:}\vspace{4pt}

prefix S              toggle synchronize-panes (type in all)\\
prefix C              customize-mode\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} BUILT-IN LAYOUTS (Alt+number):}\vspace{4pt}

prefix Alt-1          even-horizontal\\
prefix Alt-2          even-vertical\\
prefix Alt-3          main-horizontal\\
prefix Alt-4          main-vertical\\
prefix Alt-5          tiled\\
prefix Alt-6          main-horizontal-mirrored\\
prefix Alt-7          main-vertical-mirrored\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} WINDOW ROTATION:}\vspace{4pt}

prefix Ctrl-o         rotate window panes\\
prefix Alt-o          rotate window panes (reverse)\\

Synchronize-panes (prefix S) sends keystrokes to ALL panes.\\
Perfect for running the same command across many servers.\\

\begin{codebox}
// sixteen panes is not chaos\\
// sixteen panes is the wizard's dashboard\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{16pt}

\section{Tmux Prefix Keys: Special Operations}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} TMUX PREFIX KEYS: SPECIAL OPERATIONS}\vspace{6pt}

multi-pane execution, URL picking, buffers, plugins.\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} MULTI-PANE EXECUTION:}\vspace{4pt}

prefix Space          run command in all panes (single)\\
prefix v              run command in all panes (multi)\\
prefix b              open URL/path in all panes\\
prefix g              google search in all panes\\

These source \textbf{\$ZPWR/scripts/allPanes.zsh} with different modes.\\
Space -> single mode (one command per pane)\\
v     -> multi mode (batch operations)\\
b     -> single open (open URL in each pane)\\
g     -> single google (search in each pane)\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} URL HANDLING:}\vspace{4pt}

prefix e              fzf URL picker -> open\\
prefix u              fzf URL picker -> search\\

Both use tmux-fzf-url plugin with 30s timeout.\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} PASTE \& BUFFERS:}\vspace{4pt}

prefix P              paste buffer\\
prefix ]              paste buffer (bracketed)\\
prefix =              choose-buffer (fzf style)\\
prefix \#              list buffers\\
prefix Ctrl-v         paste from system clipboard\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} COPY MODE:}\vspace{4pt}

prefix [              enter copy mode\\
prefix PgUp           enter copy mode and page up\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} PLUGIN MANAGEMENT (TPM):}\vspace{4pt}

prefix I              install plugins\\
prefix U              update plugins\\
prefix Alt-u          clean unused plugins\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} SEND PREFIX:}\vspace{4pt}

prefix Ctrl-a         send prefix key to inner tmux\\
prefix Ctrl-]         send literal Ctrl-]\\

Use prefix Ctrl-a when nesting tmux sessions.\\
The outer session captures prefix, Ctrl-a forwards it.\\

\begin{codebox}
// buffers are the wizard's memory\\
// every copy is a spell stored for later\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{16pt}

\section{Tmux Copy Mode (vi)}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} TMUX COPY MODE (VI BINDINGS)}\vspace{6pt}

scrollback navigation, selection, copy, search. pure vi.\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} ENTER/EXIT:}\vspace{4pt}

prefix [              enter copy mode\\
q                     cancel and exit copy mode\\
Escape                clear selection\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} SELECTION \& COPY:}\vspace{4pt}

v                     begin selection\\
V                     select entire line\\
Ctrl-v               toggle rectangle selection\\
Space                 begin selection (alternate)\\
y                     copy selection to clipboard (no clear)\\
Enter                 copy selection to clipboard and cancel\\
D                     copy to end of line and cancel\\
A                     append selection and cancel\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} NAVIGATION:}\vspace{4pt}

h/j/k/l              cursor movement\\
Ctrl-h/j/k/l         move cursor 4 cells at a time\\
w/b/e                word forward/backward/end\\
W/B/E                WORD (space-delimited) movement\\
0 / \$                start/end of line\\
\textasciicircum{}                     first non-blank character\\
g / G                top / bottom of history\\
H / M / L            top / middle / bottom of screen\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} SCROLLING:}\vspace{4pt}

Ctrl-u / Ctrl-d      half page up / down\\
Ctrl-b / Ctrl-f      full page up / down\\
Ctrl-y / Ctrl-e      scroll up / down one line\\
J / K                scroll down / up one line\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} SEARCH:}\vspace{4pt}

/                     search forward (incremental)\\
?                     search backward (incremental)\\
n / N                next / previous match\\
*                     search forward for word under cursor\\
\#                     search backward for word under cursor\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} \textbf{ZPWR} EXTENSIONS:}\vspace{4pt}

s                     copy + google search selection\\
x                     copy + open URL selection\\
z                     copy + google search selection\\
RightClick            copy + google search selection\\

Copy goes to system clipboard via reattach-to-user-namespace pbcopy.\\
\textbf{ZPWR} extends vi copy mode with instant google/open actions.\\

\begin{codebox}
// in copy mode the wizard moves through time\\
// scrollback is archaeology, search is divination\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{16pt}

\section{Zsh Insert Mode: Basic \& Movement}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} ZSH INSERT MODE: BASIC \& MOVEMENT}\vspace{6pt}

the primary editing mode. where commands are born.\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} LINE MOVEMENT:}\vspace{4pt}

Ctrl-A                beginning-of-line\\
Ctrl-E                end-of-line\\
Ctrl-O                EOL or next tab stop\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} EDITING:}\vspace{4pt}

Ctrl-U                clear entire line\\
Ctrl-W                delete word backward (autopair)\\
Ctrl-H                delete char backward (autopair)\\
Ctrl-Y                change surrounding quotes\\
Ctrl-Z                undo\\
Ctrl-R                redo\\
Ctrl-Q                duplicate last word\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} \textbf{ZPWR} SPECIAL:}\vspace{4pt}

Space                 zpwr supernatural expand (aliases+globs)\\
Ctrl-@                zpwr expand + terminate space\\
Ctrl-M (Enter)        zpwr magic enter (show status on empty)\\
.                     zpwr rationalize dot (.. -> ../..)\\
Ctrl-B                zpwr clipboard paste\\
Ctrl-S                git add commit push (no check)\\
Ctrl-K                zsh-learn-Learn (flashcard)\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} COMPLETION \& FZF:}\vspace{4pt}

Tab (Ctrl-I)          fzf-completion\\
Ctrl-D                list-choices\\
Ctrl-L                clear-screen\\
Ctrl-T                fzf file widget\\
Alt-c                 fzf cd widget\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} HISTORY:}\vspace{4pt}

Ctrl-N                down-history\\
Ctrl-P                up-history\\
Up/Down arrows        history substring search up/down\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} MODE SWITCHING:}\vspace{4pt}

Escape                enter vi command mode\\
jf / fj              enter vi command mode (chord escape)\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} SURROUND \& PAIRS:}\vspace{4pt}

" ' ( [ \{ \textbackslash{}`          auto-pair/surround insert\\
) ] \}                 autopair close\\
Backspace             autopair-aware delete\\

Space is the most powerful key: it expands aliases,\\
global aliases, and abbreviations before inserting.\\

\begin{codebox}
// insert mode is where spells are typed\\
// every keystroke is an incantation\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{16pt}

\section{Zsh Insert Mode: Ctrl-F \& Ctrl-V Chords}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} ZSH INSERT MODE: CTRL-F \& CTRL-V CHORDS}\vspace{6pt}

two-key combos that unlock the full zpwr arsenal.\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} CTRL-F CHORDS (fzf \& actions):}\vspace{4pt}

Ctrl-F Ctrl-D         pipe buffer into fzf\\
Ctrl-F Ctrl-F         cd + vim fzf file search (accept)\\
Ctrl-F Ctrl-G         google search\\
Ctrl-F Ctrl-H         lsof into fzf\\
Ctrl-F Ctrl-I         ag (silver searcher) into fzf\\
Ctrl-F Ctrl-J         zpwr verbs widget (accept)\\
Ctrl-F Ctrl-K         alternate quotes around buffer\\
Ctrl-F Ctrl-L         list choices\\
Ctrl-F Ctrl-M         zzcomplete\\
Ctrl-F Ctrl-N         zpwr verbs widget (browse)\\
Ctrl-F Ctrl-O         open URL from buffer\\
Ctrl-F Ctrl-P         basic sed substitution\\
Ctrl-F Ctrl-R         wrap buffer as variable\\
Ctrl-F Ctrl-S         git diff check (gacp)\\
Ctrl-F Ctrl-V         edit command line in \$\textbf{EDITOR}\\
Ctrl-F j              zpwr verbs widget (accept)\\
Ctrl-F n              zpwr verbs widget (browse)\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} CTRL-V CHORDS (vim/fzf/navigation):}\vspace{4pt}

Ctrl-V Ctrl-@         vim fzf (open file in vim)\\
Ctrl-V Space          vim fzf (open file in vim)\\
Ctrl-V Ctrl-F         fasd fzf (frecency file open)\\
Ctrl-V Ctrl-G         fzf cd widget\\
Ctrl-V Ctrl-K         emacs fzf\\
Ctrl-V Ctrl-L         z fzf (frecency dirs)\\
Ctrl-V Ctrl-N         vim fzf sudo\\
Ctrl-V Ctrl-O         fzf tab complete\\
Ctrl-V Ctrl-P         sudo command line toggle\\
Ctrl-V Ctrl-R         history search multi-word\\
Ctrl-V Ctrl-S         z fzf (alternate)\\
Ctrl-V Ctrl-V         vim all files widget (accept)\\
Ctrl-V Ctrl-Z         fzf history widget\\
Ctrl-V ,              fzf environment variables\\
Ctrl-V .              fzf all keybindings\\

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} Ctrl-V //             locate fzf}

Ctrl-V /.             locate fzf + edit\\
Ctrl-V ;              fzf surround\\
Ctrl-V c              fzf git commits\\
Ctrl-V k              fzf vim keybindings\\
Ctrl-V m              vim all files widget (browse)\\
Ctrl-V v              vim all files widget (accept)\\

Ctrl-F is the action chord: search, edit, google, diff.\\
Ctrl-V is the vim/fzf chord: open files, browse, navigate.\\

\begin{codebox}
// chords are the wizard's combos\\
// two keys unlock what single keys cannot reach\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{16pt}

\section{Zsh Visual \& Menu Select Modes}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} ZSH VISUAL \& MENU SELECT MODES}\vspace{6pt}

text objects, selection, and completion menu navigation.\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} \textbf{VISUAL} MODE (enter with v/V in vicmd):}\vspace{4pt}

Escape                deactivate region\\
j / k                move selection down / up\\
o                     exchange point and mark\\
p                     put replace selection\\
x                     delete selection\\
u                     downcase selection\\
U                     upcase selection\\
\textasciitilde{}                     swap case of selection\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} TEXT OBJECTS (a = around, i = inner):}\vspace{4pt}

a" / i"              select around/inner double quotes\\
a' / i'              select around/inner single quotes\\
a\textbackslash{}` / i\textbackslash{}`              select around/inner backticks\\
a( / i(              select around/inner parentheses\\
a[ / i[              select around/inner brackets\\
a\{ / i\{              select around/inner braces\\
a< / i<              select around/inner angle brackets\\
aB / iB              select around/inner block\\
aw / iw              select a word / in word\\
aW / iW              select a blank word / in blank word\\
aa / ia              select a shell word / in shell word\\

Extended quote chars also work as text objects:\\
+ , - . / : ; = @ | \textbackslash{}\textbackslash{} are all valid quote delimiters.\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} MENU SELECT MODE (during completion):}\vspace{4pt}

Ctrl-J / Ctrl-K       move down / up in menu\\
Ctrl-H / Ctrl-L       move left / right in menu\\
Tab / Ctrl-I          move forward (next item)\\
Ctrl-S / Shift-Tab    reverse menu complete\\
Ctrl-@ (Ctrl-Space)   accept line\\
Ctrl-D                accept and menu complete (stay open)\\
Ctrl-F                accept and infer next\\
Ctrl-M (Enter)        accept line (.accept-line)\\
Ctrl-V                insert mode within menu\\
Ctrl-N / Ctrl-P       forward / backward word in menu\\
Ctrl-X                incremental search forward in menu\\
?                     incremental search backward in menu\\
.                     self-insert (exit menu + type dot)\\
Backspace             undo last menu selection\\

Menu select uses hjkl-style navigation with Ctrl prefix.\\
Ctrl-D is key: accept current match but keep menu open.\\

\begin{codebox}
// visual mode is precision surgery\\
// select only what you need, transform only what you touch\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{16pt}

\section{Vim Normal Mode Highlights}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} VIM NORMAL MODE: ZPWR HIGHLIGHTS}\vspace{6pt}

leader mappings, fzf integration, tmux synergy.\\
leader key is Space. only zpwr-specific bindings listed.\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} FILE \& BUFFER (Space prefix):}\vspace{4pt}

Space w               :w! (force write)\\
Space e               :q! (force quit)\\
Space q               :qa! (quit all)\\
Space wq              :wq! (write and quit)\\
Space n / Space p     next / prev buffer\\
Space an / Space ap   next / prev in arglist\\
Space Tab             alternate or next buffer\\
Space t               new tab\\
Space s / Space v     horizontal / vertical split\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} FZF INTEGRATION (Space prefix):}\vspace{4pt}

Space f               :Files! (fzf files)\\
Space b               :Buffers! (fzf buffers)\\
Space j               :Lines! (fzf lines)\\
Space ag              :Ag (silver searcher)\\
Space aa              :Agg (ag variant)\\
Space rg              :Rg (ripgrep)\\
Space z               :Commits! (fzf git commits)\\
Space ;               :Commands! (fzf commands)\\
Space ,               :FZFMaps (fzf all mappings)\\
Space ke / , / m / i  fzf keys / maps / nmap / imap\\
Space ta / ma / env  fzf tags / marks / env vars\\
Space / / .           locate all / colorscheme picker\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} HISTORY (Space prefix):}\vspace{4pt}

Space hh              :History! (fzf file history)\\
Space h/              :History/! (fzf search history)\\
Space h:              :History:! (fzf command history)\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} SEARCH \& REPLACE (Space prefix):}\vspace{4pt}

Space r               replace word under cursor (whole file)\\
Space g               global substitute word under cursor\\
Space x               repeat last substitution on line\\
n / N                 next / prev search (centered)\\
z/                    toggle auto-highlight word under cursor\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} GIT \& TMUX:}\vspace{4pt}

Space hs              GitGutter stage hunk\\
Space hu              GitGutter undo hunk\\
Space hp              GitGutter preview hunk\\
{[}c / ]c              prev / next git hunk\\
Space vj              save + TmuxRepeat file\\
Space os / ox / oc   google / open URL / copy word\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} MINIMAP \& COMMENTS:}\vspace{4pt}

Space mm              open minimap\\
Space mt              toggle minimap\\
Space cc              NERDCommenter comment\\
Space c Space         NERDCommenter toggle\\
Space cu              NERDCommenter uncomment\\

\begin{codebox}
// the leader key is Space because power needs room\\
// every binding is one thought away from execution\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{16pt}

\section{Vim Insert \& Visual Mode + Keybinding Search}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} VIM INSERT \& VISUAL MODE + KEYBINDING SEARCH}\vspace{6pt}

vim mode highlights and how to find any keybinding.\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} VIM INSERT MODE HIGHLIGHTS:}\vspace{4pt}

Ctrl-A                jump to first non-blank (like \textasciicircum{})\\
Ctrl-E                end of line or dismiss popup\\
Ctrl-D                delete char forward or default\\
Ctrl-F                move right or scroll\\
Ctrl-S                isurround (surround insert)\\
Ctrl-G s / S          isurround / ISurround (line)\\
Ctrl-Tab              list ultisnips snippets\\
Shift-Tab             SuperTab backward completion\\
Alt-d                 delete word forward\\
" ' ( ) [ ] \textbackslash{}` \{ \}    delimitMate auto-pairing\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} VIM \textbf{VISUAL} MODE HIGHLIGHTS:}\vspace{4pt}

Space r               replace word in selection range\\
Space g               global substitute in selection range\\
Space x               repeat last sub on selected lines\\
Space " ' \textbackslash{}` ( [ \{    surround selection with quote/bracket\\
Space b               copy selection to tmux buffer\\
Space = / Space -     grow / shrink selection (4 lines)\\
J / K                move selected lines down / up\\
Y                     yank and move to end\\
< / >                indent / outdent (stay in visual)\\
S                     vim-surround visual surround\\
go                    copy selection + open as URL\\
gs                    copy selection + google search\\
Space vl / vk / vj   TmuxRepeat repl / visual / file\\
Space em / ev / ef   extract method / variable / fold\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} SNEAK \& MOTION:}\vspace{4pt}

s / S                sneak forward / backward (2-char)\\
f / F / t / T        sneak-enhanced find char\\
; / ,                repeat / reverse last sneak/find\\
w / b / e            CamelCaseMotion word movement\\


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} =}\vspace{6pt}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} HOW TO SEARCH KEYBINDINGS:}\vspace{4pt}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} =}\vspace{6pt}

zpwr allsearch        search ALL keybindings in fzf\\
zpwr vimsearch        search vim keybindings in fzf\\
zpwr zshsearch        search zsh keybindings in fzf\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} KEYBINDING CACHE FILES:}\vspace{4pt}

\textbf{\$ZPWR\_LOCAL/zpwrAllKeybindings.txt}\\
\textbf{\$ZPWR\_LOCAL/zpwr}\{Vim,Zsh,Tmux\}Keybindings.txt\\


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} REGENERATE:}\vspace{4pt}

zpwr regenkeybindings  regenerate all keybinding caches\\

Cache files are auto-generated. Run regenkeybindings after\\
adding new bindings to refresh the searchable index.\\

\begin{codebox}
// the wizard does not memorize 4000 keybindings\\
// the wizard searches them at the speed of thought\\
// fzf is the oracle, the cache is the grimoire\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{16pt}

\chapter{TMUX DEEP DIVE}


\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=0.85\textwidth]{/Users/wizard/.zpwr/docs/screenshots/art_mainframe.png}
\end{center}

\section{Tmux Layout Save \& Restore}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} TMUX LAYOUT SAVE \& RESTORE}\vspace{6pt}

Your pane arrangement, preserved forever.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE PROBLEM}\vspace{4pt}

You spent 20 minutes splitting panes, resizing them, cd-ing into the right directories. Then tmux crashes. Or you reboot. Or you accidentally kill the session. All that layout work? Gone. Every time.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE SOLUTION}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr tmuxsave dev             \# save layout as 'dev'\\
zpwr tmuxload dev             \# restore it later\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} WHAT GETS SAVED}\vspace{4pt}

Windows ............... names and count Pane splits ........... exact geometry via select-layout Directories ........... per-pane working directory Running commands ...... full args from process tree Window options ........ synchronize-panes, auto-rename Session options ....... non-plugin tmux settings Active pane/window .... cursor position restored


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} MANAGEMENT}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr tmuxsave                 \# save with timestamp name\\
zpwr tmuxsave --list          \# list saved layouts\\
zpwr tmuxsave --delete dev    \# remove a layout\\
zpwr tmuxload                 \# fzf picker (no args)\\
zpwr tmuxload dev mywork      \# restore as session 'mywork'\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} KEYBINDING}\vspace{4pt}

Prefix W                      \# save layout (tmux keybinding)


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} ALIASES}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr layoutsave  = zpwr tmuxsave\\
zpwr layoutload  = zpwr tmuxload\\
\end{codebox}

Layouts are stored as self-contained zsh scripts in \textbf{\$ZPWR\_LOCAL/layouts/.} You can edit them by hand, version control them, or share them with your team.

PROTIP: Save your layout before experimenting. If you break everything, one command brings it back.


\vspace{16pt}


\chapter{MONITORING \& AUTOMATION}


\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=0.85\textwidth]{/Users/wizard/.zpwr/docs/screenshots/zpwr_watch_help.png}
\end{center}

\section{Live Dashboard \& Sparklines}


\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=0.8\textwidth]{/Users/wizard/.zpwr/docs/screenshots/zpwr_bench_help.png}
\end{center}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} LIVE DASHBOARD \& SPARKLINES}\vspace{6pt}

Your shell's vital signs, in real time.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} zpwr top}\vspace{4pt}

A live-updating dashboard of your shell's resource usage. Runs in alternate screen buffer. Press q to quit.

\begin{codebox}
zpwr top       \# refresh every 2s\\
zpwr top 1     \# fast refresh\\
zpwr top 5     \# slow refresh\\
zpwr dashboard \# same verb\\
zpwr live      \# same verb\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} WHAT IT SHOWS}\vspace{4pt}

Memory ............ RSS bar graph, virtual memory Shell objects ..... functions, aliases, completions, params Delta tracking .... changes between refreshes in yellow Loaded modules .... all zsh modules currently loaded Paths ............ fpath, path, named dirs, dir stack Context .......... git branch, tmux info, startup time Top 5 functions .. largest functions with size bars Top 5 paths ...... longest \textbf{PATH} entries


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} SPARKLINES}\vspace{4pt}

Startup time history: last 40 shell starts Color-coded: green=fast yellow=mid red=slow Shows min/max/avg stats below the graph.

Commit velocity: commits per day over 30 days Visualizes your development pace as a mini bar chart.

Startup times are logged automatically on each shell init to \textbf{\$ZPWR\_LOCAL/startup\_history.log.}


\vspace{16pt}

\section{Matrix: The Full Experience}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} MATRIX: THE FULL EXPERIENCE}\vspace{6pt}

8 acts, 6 characters, and your ecosystem raining down


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE STORY}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr matrix               \# 4-act story + rain\\
zpwr matrix --extended     \# full 8-act saga\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE CHARACTERS}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr matrix --cast         \# show character bios\\
\end{codebox}

Null Pointer .... protagonist, zpwr operator Segfault ........ bash loyalist in recovery Chmod777 ........ reckless, sudo for everything

\begin{codebox}
DevNull ......... silent assassin\\
\end{codebox}

Chad Electron ... MegaCorp VP, 64GB for Slack The Kernel ...... mythical elder, speaks in dmesg


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} \textbf{VISUAL} FX}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr matrix --noir         \# monochrome green\\
zpwr matrix --vhs          \# VHS tracking distortion\\
zpwr matrix --crt          \# CRT scanlines\\
zpwr matrix --glitch       \# extra corruption\\
zpwr matrix --sound        \# terminal bells\\
zpwr matrix --no-fx        \# disable all FX\\
zpwr matrix -c 10          \# chaos level 1-10\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} PLAYBACK CONTROL}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr matrix -s 7           \# speed 1-9\\
zpwr matrix --turbo        \# skip all pauses\\
zpwr matrix -a 5           \# jump to act 5\\
zpwr matrix -r             \# skip story, rain only\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} MULTIPLAYER}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr matrix --battle       \# 2-player tmux typing battle\\
\end{codebox}

Player 1 (Null Pointer) vs Player 2 (Chad Electron). Type zpwr commands faster than your opponent. HP bars, taunts, and a winner-takes-all endgame. Requires tmux. Auto-splits into two panes.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} INFO}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
zpwr matrix --stats        \# ecosystem stats\\
zpwr matrix --credits      \# end credits roll\\
\end{codebox}
