\chapter{THE END}


\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=0.85\textwidth]{/Users/wizard/.zpwr/docs/screenshots/art_hack_the_planet.png}
\end{center}

\section{The Epilogue: You Are the Wizard}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} THE EPILOGUE: YOU ARE THE WIZARD}\vspace{6pt}

The terminal bows to you.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} WHAT YOU'VE LEARNED}\vspace{4pt}

From keybindings to kernel. Every chapter, every verb. Autoloaded functions. Tmux pipelines. Fzf integration. Vim execution. Perl oneliners. Systemd services. 32-pane REPL layouts. Cross-platform installers. A 24-hour updater loop. A 60-file test suite. A colorization stack five tools deep. And a startup banner delivered by a rainbow pony.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE 5 COMMANDS TO MEMORIZE}\vspace{4pt}

zpwr verbs    list every zpwr subcommand zpwr doctor   run environment health check diagnostic zpwr bench    benchmark startup with percentiles zpwr wizard   interactive guided tour (you're here) zpwr study    split-pane learning: book left, shell right Five commands. That's your entire onboarding.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} HOW TO ADD YOUR OWN VERBS}\vspace{4pt}

1. Create an autoload function in \textbf{\$ZPWR/autoload/common/} 2. Add to \textbf{ZPWR\_VERBS} in \textbf{\$ZPWR\_ENV/zpwr.zsh} Format: \textbf{ZPWR\_VERBS}[myverb]='myFunc=description' 3. Reload: exec zsh. Your verb is live.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} HOW TO EXTEND THE WIZARD}\vspace{4pt}

Add a new page\_NNN.zsh to \textbf{\$ZPWR\_INSTALL/wizard\_pages/} Follow the format: PAGE\_TITLE, PAGE\_CHAPTER, PAGE\_CONTENT(). The wizard auto-discovers pages. No registration needed.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} HOW TO CONTRIBUTE}\vspace{4pt}

Fork github.com/MenkeTechnologies/zpwr Add your feature. Write tests. Submit a PR. The codebase is the documentation. Read it.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} THE \textbf{ZPWR} PHILOSOPHY}\vspace{4pt}

Verbs, not scripts.  Discoverability over memorization. Speed over bloat.    Fallbacks over hard dependencies. Convention over config.  Your shell should just work.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} ONE LAST THING}\vspace{4pt}

Run zpwr about to see the zpwr banner. Then open a new terminal. Watch the pony greet you. You are the wizard now. The terminal is yours.


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} END OF TRANSMISSION}\vspace{6pt}

{\small\itshape\color{dimtext} // \textbf{ZPWR} WIZARD ENCYCLOPEDIA v1.0 // SIGNAL LOST //}

May your shell be fast, your pipes be clean, and your exit codes always zero.


\vspace{16pt}


\chapter{HEALTH \& DIAGNOSTICS}


\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=0.85\textwidth]{/Users/wizard/.zpwr/docs/screenshots/zpwr_doctor_help.png}
\end{center}

\section{Expansion Stats Dashboard}


\vspace{10pt}
{\large\bfseries\color{neoncyan} EXPANSION STATS DASHBOARD}\vspace{6pt}

Your aliases are working for you — here's the proof.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} zpwrExpandStats}\vspace{4pt}

Every time zsh-expand fires — alias, global alias, suffix alias, self-ref escape, native glob/hist, or spelling correction — it logs the event. zpwrExpandStats reads that log and shows you a ranked dashboard.

\begin{codebox}
zpwrExpandStats            \# show full dashboard\\
zpwrExpandStats -h         \# help with all options\\
zpwrExpandStats -t 10      \# top 10 aliases\\
zpwrExpandStats -w 80      \# wider box (80 cols)\\
zpwrExpandStats -r         \# reset all stats\\
zpwrExpandStats -f FILE    \# custom stats file\\
\end{codebox}


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} WHAT IT TRACKS}\vspace{4pt}

By trigger ......... space expansions vs history expansions By type ............ alias, global, suffix, escape, native Corrections ........ spelling fixes applied Total expansions ... how many times the engine fired Keystrokes saved ... chars you didn't have to type Top aliases ........ ranked bar chart with expansions shown


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} HOW IT WORKS}\vspace{4pt}

The zsh-expand plugin hooks into the zle accept-line widget. Before each command runs, it expands aliases, globals, and suffixes inline. Each expansion is logged to \textbf{\$ZPWR\_LOCAL/zpwr-expand-stats.dat} with the trigger type, expansion type, and original alias name.


\vspace{12pt}
{\bfseries\color{neonyellow} CONFIG}\vspace{4pt}

\begin{codebox}
ZPWR\_EXPAND\_STATS\_FILE     \# override stats file path\\
ZPWR\_EXPAND\_STATS\_TOP      \# default top N (default: 20)\\
\end{codebox}

Every alias that fires is a keystroke investment paying dividends. This dashboard shows your ROI.


\vspace{16pt}
